<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2003 Atlantic hurricane season</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<tr>
<td class="hlist noprint nowrap" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;"><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">Atlantic hurricane seasons</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/2001_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2001 Atlantic hurricane season">2001</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2002 Atlantic hurricane season">2002</a>, <b>2003</b>, <a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>2003 Atlantic hurricane season</b> was an active <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Atlantic hurricane season">Atlantic hurricane season</a> with <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical activity</a> before and after the official bounds of the season – the first such occurrence in 49 years. The season produced 21 <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a>, of which 16 developed into named storms; seven cyclones attained hurricane status, of which three reached <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane status</a>. With sixteen storms, the season was tied for the sixth most active <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic_hurricane_seasons" title="List of Atlantic hurricane seasons">Atlantic hurricane season</a> on record. The strongest hurricane of the season was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isabel" title="Hurricane Isabel">Hurricane Isabel</a>, which reached <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">Category 5</a> status on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale</a> northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>; Isabel later struck <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> as a Category 2 hurricane, causing $3.6 billion in damage (2003 USD, $4.69 billion 2017 USD) and a total of 51 deaths across the Mid-Atlantic region of the United States.</p>
<p>The season began with <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)">Subtropical Storm Ana</a> on April 20, prior to the official start of the season; the bounds of the season are from June 1 to November 30, which conventionally delimit the period of each year when most tropical cyclones form in the Atlantic basin. In early September, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fabian" title="Hurricane Fabian">Hurricane Fabian</a> struck <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 3</a> hurricane, where it was the worst hurricane since <a href="/wiki/1926_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1926 Atlantic hurricane season">1926</a>; on the island it caused four deaths and $300 million in damage (2003 USD, $391 million 2017 USD). <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Juan" title="Hurricane Juan">Hurricane Juan</a> caused considerable destruction to <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, particularly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax Regional Municipality, Nova Scotia">Halifax</a>, as a Category 2 hurricane, the first hurricane of significant strength to hit the province since <a href="/wiki/1893_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1893 Atlantic hurricane season">1893</a>. Additionally, Hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Claudette_(2003)" title="Hurricane Claudette (2003)">Claudette</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Erika_(2003)" title="Hurricane Erika (2003)">Erika</a> struck Texas and Mexico, respectively, as minimal hurricanes.</p>
<p></p>

</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-season_outlook">Pre-season outlook</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-season outlook">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On May 19, prior to the start of the season, <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">NOAA</a> forecasters issued a 55% probability of above normal activity. The forecasters predicted 11–15 tropical storms, 6–9 of those becoming hurricanes, and 2–4 of those hurricanes reaching at least Category 3 strength on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale</a>. The above normal activity predicted was due to the likelihood of <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Niña">La Niña</a> developing in the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_May_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_May-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Noted hurricane expert Dr. <a href="/wiki/William_M._Gray" title="William M. Gray">William M. Gray</a> on April 4 predicted twelve named storms, with eight reaching hurricane strength and three of the eight reaching Category 3 strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grapril_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grapril-3">[3]</a></sup> The prediction issued on May 30 was similar, increasing the named storms to fourteen. The synoptic pattern of the season prior to June 1 resembled other previous seasons, with the <a href="/wiki/1952_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1952 Atlantic hurricane season">1952</a>, <a href="/wiki/1954_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1954 Atlantic hurricane season">1954</a>, <a href="/wiki/1964_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1964 Atlantic hurricane season">1964</a>, <a href="/wiki/1966_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1966 Atlantic hurricane season">1966</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1998_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1998 Atlantic hurricane season">1998</a> seasons considered the best analogs for the season. The prediction also included a 68% probability for a hurricane landfall along the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grmay_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grmay-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mid-season_outlook">Mid-season outlook</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mid-season outlook">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 6, Dr. Gray announced he had maintained his previous prediction; with an active start of the season, the rest of the season was forecast to have been only slightly above average, due to an anticipated overall less favorable environment across the Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_Aug_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_Aug-5">[5]</a></sup> A day later, NOAA released an updated prediction as well, with a 60% probability of above normal activity, with 12–15 named storms, 7–9 hurricanes, and 3–4 major hurricanes expected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_Aug_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_Aug-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>A normal season, as defined by NOAA, has 6–14 tropical storms, 4–8 of which reach hurricane strength, and 1–3 of those reaching Category 3 strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPC_BG_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPC_BG-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_summary">Season summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Season summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2003 Atlantic hurricane season">Timeline of the 2003 Atlantic hurricane season</a></div>
<center>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_b9bb7ab390b3b0e6f4f39f030bd3eef1" name="timeline_b9bb7ab390b3b0e6f4f39f030bd3eef1">
<area alt="Tropical Storm Odette (2003)" coords="702,23,799,43" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Odette_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Odette (2003)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Nicholas (2003)" coords="577,9,685,30" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Nicholas_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Nicholas (2003)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Larry (2003)" coords="530,104,622,124" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Larry_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Larry (2003)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Kate (2003)" coords="533,90,619,111" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Kate_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Kate (2003)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Juan" coords="511,77,597,97" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Juan" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Juan"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Isabel" coords="483,50,580,70" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isabel" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Isabel"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Henri (2003)" coords="452,36,544,57" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Henri_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Henri (2003)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Grace (2003)" coords="436,23,527,43" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Grace_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Grace (2003)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Fabian" coords="452,9,550,30" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fabian" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Fabian"/>
<area alt="Tropical Depression Nine (2003)" coords="405,117,491,138" href="/wiki/Tropical_Depression_Nine_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Depression Nine (2003)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Erika (2003)" coords="391,104,483,124" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Erika_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Erika (2003)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Claudette (2003)" coords="305,50,419,70" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Claudette_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Claudette (2003)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Bill (2003)" coords="264,36,350,57" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bill_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Bill (2003)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)" coords="72,9,153,30" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)"/>
<area alt="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale" coords="602,195,804,215" href="/wiki/Saffir%2DSimpson_Hurricane_Scale" shape="rect" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale"/></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/b9bb7ab390b3b0e6f4f39f030bd3eef1.png" usemap="#timeline_b9bb7ab390b3b0e6f4f39f030bd3eef1"/></div>
</center>
<p>The official beginning of the season was on June 1, 2003,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61two_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-61two-8">[8]</a></sup> though <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)">Subtropical Storm Ana</a> formed on April 20, well before the start to the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anatcr_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-anatcr-9">[9]</a></sup> Starting at the official start of the season, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> began issuing five-day forecasts, extending from the three-day forecasts issued since 1964. Officials conducted tests during the previous two seasons, indicating the new five-day forecasts would be as accurate as the three-day forecasts were 15 years earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The tropics were active and well ahead of climatology in the early portion of the season, with the seventh tropical depression forming by the end of July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The season officially ended on November 30, 2003,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61two_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-61two-8">[8]</a></sup> although tropical storms <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Odette_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Odette (2003)">Odette</a> and Peter developed in early December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odettetcr_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-odettetcr-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptcr_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-ptcr-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The season is one of only six with a storm before and after the official bounds of the season; the others are <a href="/wiki/1887_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1887 Atlantic hurricane season">1887</a>, <a href="/wiki/1951_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1951 Atlantic hurricane season">1951</a>, <a href="/wiki/1953_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1953 Atlantic hurricane season">1953</a>, <a href="/wiki/1954_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1954 Atlantic hurricane season">1954</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2007 Atlantic hurricane season">2007</a>. When Tropical Storm Peter formed on December 7, the season became the second on record with two December storms. The 235 days between the development of the first storm, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)">Tropical Storm Ana</a>, and the dissipation of the last storm, Peter, made the 2003 season the longest season since <a href="/wiki/1952_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1952 Atlantic hurricane season">1952</a>. The season was the eighth most active on record, behind the <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/1933_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1933 Atlantic hurricane season">1933</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2012 Atlantic hurricane season">2012</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2011 Atlantic hurricane season">2011</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2010 Atlantic hurricane season">2010</a>, <a href="/wiki/1995_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1995 Atlantic hurricane season">1995</a>, <a href="/wiki/1887_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1887 Atlantic hurricane season">1887</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1969_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1969 Atlantic hurricane season">1969</a> seasons, and tied with the <a href="/wiki/1936_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1936 Atlantic hurricane season">1936</a> and <a href="/wiki/2008_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2008 Atlantic hurricane season">2008</a> seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>No cyclones in the season had a significant impact on South America or Central America. However, a total of eight tropical cyclones made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> on Mexico from either the Atlantic or the Pacific Ocean, which was the greatest total since the record of nine in <a href="/wiki/1971_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1971 Atlantic hurricane season">1971</a>. A total of seven deaths occurred in Mexico from Atlantic hurricanes. Much of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> did not receive significant impact from tropical cyclones during the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003wmo_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-2003wmo-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fabiandamage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Fabiandamage.jpg/220px-Fabiandamage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Fabiandamage.jpg/330px-Fabiandamage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Fabiandamage.jpg/440px-Fabiandamage.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fabiandamage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damage from Hurricane Fabian on Bermuda</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Six tropical cyclones made landfall along the coast of the United States during the season, including two hurricanes. The first, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Claudette_(2003)" title="Hurricane Claudette (2003)">Claudette</a>, caused locally heavy damage in southeastern Texas in July; two deaths were reported in the state, while earlier in its duration it caused an indirect death from rough waves in Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-claudettetcr_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-claudettetcr-16">[16]</a></sup> In September, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isabel" title="Hurricane Isabel">Hurricane Isabel</a> caused deaths and damage from North Carolina through southern Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-istcr_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-istcr-17">[17]</a></sup> The worst damage from the hurricane occurred in Virginia, where it was the costliest disaster in the history of the state;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cws_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-cws-18">[18]</a></sup> there, damage totaled $1.85 billion (2003 USD, $2.41 billion 2017 USD), and there were 32 fatalities, ten of which were caused directly by the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-istcr_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-istcr-17">[17]</a></sup> Hurricane Isabel caused deaths in seven states and one Canadian province, and about 6 million people were left without power as a result of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assess_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-assess-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several cyclones impacted <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> during the season, most significantly <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fabian" title="Hurricane Fabian">Hurricane Fabian</a>. On the island, its passage proved to be the costliest and resulted in the first death since a hurricane in <a href="/wiki/1926_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1926 Atlantic hurricane season">1926</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mostdaming_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-mostdaming-20">[20]</a></sup> The hurricane killed four on the island when its strong waves and storm surge washed two cars off <a href="/wiki/The_Causeway,_Bermuda" title="The Causeway, Bermuda">the causeway</a> between <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Parish,_Bermuda" title="St. George's Parish, Bermuda">St. George's Parish</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._David%27s_Island,_Bermuda" title="St. David's Island, Bermuda">St. David's Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Damage from the hurricane totaled $300 million (2003 USD, $391 million 2017 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fabiantcr_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-fabiantcr-22">[22]</a></sup> Elsewhere, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Juan" title="Hurricane Juan">Hurricane Juan</a> was considered among the most damaging in the history of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax</a>, Nova Scotia, where strong winds downed thousands of trees and left low-lying areas flooded from a record storm surge to the city. The hurricane caused a total of eight deaths and damage estimated at $200 million (2003 <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">CAD</a>, $150 million 2003 USD, $195 million 2017 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-summary_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-summary-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Ana">Tropical Storm Ana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Ana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:111.1455.rgb143.jpg"><img alt="111.1455.rgb143.jpg" data-file-height="637" data-file-width="671" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/111.1455.rgb143.jpg/150px-111.1455.rgb143.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/111.1455.rgb143.jpg/225px-111.1455.rgb143.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/111.1455.rgb143.jpg/300px-111.1455.rgb143.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ana_2003_track.png"><img alt="Ana 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ana_2003_track.png/150px-Ana_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ana_2003_track.png/225px-Ana_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ana_2003_track.png/300px-Ana_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>April 20 – April 24</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>60 mph (95 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  994 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)">Tropical Storm Ana (2003)</a></div>
<p>A non-tropical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a> developed about 240 mi (390 km) south-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> on April 18 through the interaction of an upper-level <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">trough</a> and a surface frontal <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">trough</a>. It tracked northwestward at first, then turned to the southeast. After developing centralized convection, the system developed into Subtropical Storm Ana on April 20 to the west of Bermuda. It tracked east-southeastward and organized, and on April 21 it transitioned into a tropical cyclone with peak winds of 60 mph (95 km/h), after developing an upper-level <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Physical_structure" title="Tropical cyclone">warm core</a>. Increased <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> caused fluctuations in intensity and a steady weakening trend, and on April 24 the center of Ana merged with an approaching <a href="/wiki/Cold_front" title="Cold front">cold front</a>, thus signaling the completion of <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical transition</a>. The extratropical remnants continued east-northeastward, and on April 27 the gale was absorbed within the cold front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anatcr_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-anatcr-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cyclone is most notable for being the only Atlantic tropical cyclone in the month of April, until Tropical Storm Arlene in 2017. When Ana became a Subtropical Storm, it became the second subtropical cyclone on record in the month, after a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_Storm_One_(1992)" title="Subtropical Storm One (1992)">storm in 1992</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anatcr_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-anatcr-9">[9]</a></sup> Ana dropped 2.63 in (67 mm) of rainfall in Bermuda over a period of several days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Increased swells from the storm caused two drowning deaths in southeastern <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> when a boat capsized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anatcr_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-anatcr-9">[9]</a></sup> The remnants of the storm brought light rainfall to the Azores and the United Kingdom, though no significant damage was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Two">Tropical Depression Two</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Two">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Depression_Two_(2003).jpg"><img alt="Tropical Depression Two (2003).jpg" data-file-height="482" data-file-width="642" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Tropical_Depression_Two_%282003%29.jpg/150px-Tropical_Depression_Two_%282003%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Tropical_Depression_Two_%282003%29.jpg/225px-Tropical_Depression_Two_%282003%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Tropical_Depression_Two_%282003%29.jpg/300px-Tropical_Depression_Two_%282003%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2-L_2003_track.png"><img alt="2-L 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/2-L_2003_track.png/150px-2-L_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/2-L_2003_track.png/225px-2-L_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/2-L_2003_track.png/300px-2-L_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>June 11 – June 11</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1008 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of Africa on June 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td2tcr_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-td2tcr-26">[26]</a></sup> Tracking westward at a low latitude, a disturbance along the wave axis became better organized on June 9,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> with reasonable favorable environmental conditions despite the time of year. Initially lacking a well-defined low-level circulation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> convection increased further on June 10, and the system was declared Tropical Depression Two early on June 11 in the central tropical Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td2tcr_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-td2tcr-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td2disc1_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-td2disc1-29">[29]</a></sup> The depression was at the time the third tropical cyclone on record to develop in the month of June to the east of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-June_03_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-June_03-30">[30]</a></sup> the others were <a href="/wiki/2000_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Tropical_Depression_Two" title="2000 Atlantic hurricane season">Tropical Depression Two</a> in 2000,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1979_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Ana" title="1979 Atlantic hurricane season">Ana</a> in 1979, and a <a href="/wiki/1933_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Two" title="1933 Atlantic hurricane season">storm</a> in 1933.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-June_03_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-June_03-30">[30]</a></sup> The next such system to accomplish this would be <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">Bret</a> in 2017.</p>
<p>Initially, the depression was forecast to attain tropical storm status, maintaining good <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> and some <a href="/wiki/Squall#Tropical_cyclones" title="Squall">banding features</a> around the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td2disc1_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-td2disc1-29">[29]</a></sup> Around 0900 UTC on June 11 satellite-based intensity estimates indicated the depression was near tropical storm status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td2disc2_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-td2disc2-32">[32]</a></sup> However, the convection subsequently diminished and became displaced to the northeast of the center, and late on June 11 the depression degenerated into an open tropical wave about 950 mi (1535 km) east-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td2tcr_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-td2tcr-26">[26]</a></sup> The tropical wave remained well-defined with a well-defined low-level vorticity, though strong <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> prevented tropical redevelopment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> On June 13 its remnants passed through the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, and the wave continued westward through the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Bill">Tropical Storm Bill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Bill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Bill_2003.jpg"><img alt="TS Bill 2003.jpg" data-file-height="6157" data-file-width="5892" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/TS_Bill_2003.jpg/150px-TS_Bill_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/TS_Bill_2003.jpg/225px-TS_Bill_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/TS_Bill_2003.jpg/300px-TS_Bill_2003.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bill_2003_track.png"><img alt="Bill 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bill_2003_track.png/150px-Bill_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bill_2003_track.png/225px-Bill_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bill_2003_track.png/300px-Bill_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>June 29 – July 2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>60 mph (95 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  997 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bill_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Bill (2003)">Tropical Storm Bill (2003)</a></div>
<p>Tropical Storm Bill developed from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> on June 29 to the north of the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a>. It slowly organized as it moved northward, and reached a peak of 60 mph (95 km/h) shortly before making landfall 27 mi (43 km) west of <a href="/wiki/Chauvin,_Louisiana" title="Chauvin, Louisiana">Chauvin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>. Bill quickly weakened over land, and as it accelerated to the northeast, moisture from the storm, combined with cold air from an approaching <a href="/wiki/Surface_weather_analysis" title="Surface weather analysis">cold front</a>, produced an outbreak of 34 <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a>. Bill became extratropical on July 2, and was absorbed by the cold front later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billtcr_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-billtcr-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Upon making landfall on <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, the storm produced a moderate <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a>, causing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tides" title="Tides">tidal</a> <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">flooding</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdcla_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdcla-36">[36]</a></sup> In a city in the northeastern portion of the state, the surge breached a <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">levee</a>, which flooded many homes in the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lasurge_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-lasurge-37">[37]</a></sup> Moderate winds combined with wet <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">soil</a> knocked down trees, which then hit a few houses and power lines,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billnws_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-billnws-38">[38]</a></sup> and left hundreds of thousands without <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">electric power</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billusatoday_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-billusatoday-39">[39]</a></sup> Further inland, tornadoes from the storm produced localized moderate damage. Throughout its path, Tropical Storm Bill caused around $50 million in damage (2003 USD, $65.1 million 2017 USD) and four deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billtcr_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-billtcr-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Claudette">Hurricane Claudette</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hurricane Claudette">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_claudette_july_15_2003.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane claudette july 15 2003.jpg" data-file-height="4400" data-file-width="4400" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Hurricane_claudette_july_15_2003.jpg/150px-Hurricane_claudette_july_15_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Hurricane_claudette_july_15_2003.jpg/225px-Hurricane_claudette_july_15_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Hurricane_claudette_july_15_2003.jpg/300px-Hurricane_claudette_july_15_2003.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Claudette_2003_track.png"><img alt="Claudette 2003 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Claudette_2003_track.png/150px-Claudette_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Claudette_2003_track.png/225px-Claudette_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Claudette_2003_track.png/300px-Claudette_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 8 – July 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>90 mph (150 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  979 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Claudette_(2003)" title="Hurricane Claudette (2003)">Hurricane Claudette (2003)</a></div>
<p>A well-organized <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> tracked quickly through the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> on July 7, producing tropical storm force winds but failing to attain a low-level circulation. After organizing in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, it developed into Tropical Storm Claudette to the south of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> on July 8. Its intensity fluctuated over the subsequent days, attaining hurricane status briefly on July 10 before weakening and hitting <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Morelos" title="Puerto Morelos">Puerto Morelos</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a> on July 11 as a tropical storm. The storm remained disorganized due to moderate <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, though after turning west-northwestward into an area of lighter shear, it re-attained hurricane status on July 15 off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>; it intensified quickly and made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> on <a href="/wiki/Matagorda_Island" title="Matagorda Island">Matagorda Island</a> with peak winds of 90 mph (145 km/h). It slowly weakened after moving ashore, tracking across northern <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a> before dissipating in northwestern <a href="/wiki/Chihuahua_(state)" title="Chihuahua (state)">Chihuahua</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-claudettetcr_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-claudettetcr-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The precursor cyclone caused light damage in the Lesser Antilles, and waves from the hurricane caused an indirect death off of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-claudettetcr_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-claudettetcr-16">[16]</a></sup> Widespread flooding and gusty winds destroyed or severely damaged 412 buildings in southeast Texas, with a further 1,346 buildings suffering lighter impact. The hurricane caused locally severe beach erosion along the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-setex_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-setex-40">[40]</a></sup> High winds downed many trees along the coast, causing one direct and one indirect death. Damage was estimated at $180 million (2003 USD, $234 million 2017 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-claudettetcr_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-claudettetcr-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Danny">Hurricane Danny</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hurricane Danny">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_danny_2003.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane danny 2003.jpg" data-file-height="3400" data-file-width="3400" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Hurricane_danny_2003.jpg/150px-Hurricane_danny_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Hurricane_danny_2003.jpg/225px-Hurricane_danny_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Hurricane_danny_2003.jpg/300px-Hurricane_danny_2003.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Danny_2003_track.png"><img alt="Danny 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Danny_2003_track.png/150px-Danny_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Danny_2003_track.png/225px-Danny_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Danny_2003_track.png/300px-Danny_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 16 – July 21</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>75 mph (120 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1000 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of Africa on July 9. The northern portion of the wave tracked to the west-northwest, and on July 13 an area of convection developed along the wave axis. The system slowly organized, and after a closed low-level circulation developed, the system was classified as Tropical Depression Five about 630 mi (1020 km) east of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>. It quickly organized, becoming Tropical Storm Danny a day after forming. Tracking around the periphery of an <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">anticyclone</a>, the storm moved northwestward before turning north and later northeastward. Despite being located at a high latitude, Danny continued to strengthen due to unusually warm water temperatures, and on July 19 it attained hurricane status about 525 mi (850 km) south of <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="St. John's, Newfoundland and Labrador">St. John's, Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, despite having an unusually high minimum pressure for a storm of its intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dannytcr_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-dannytcr-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">Wind shear</a> increased the next day as the hurricane turned eastward, causing a steady weakening trend that was accelerated after crossing into an area of cooler water temperatures. By July 20 the cyclone had turned to the southeast and weakened to tropical depression status, and on July 21 it degenerated into a remnant low pressure area. The remnants of Danny tracked erratically southwestward before dissipating on July 27 about 630 mi (1015 km) east of where it originally developed. There were no reports of damages or casualties associated with Danny.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dannytcr_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-dannytcr-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Six">Tropical Depression Six</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Six">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_Six_2003.jpg"><img alt="TD Six 2003.jpg" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="750" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/TD_Six_2003.jpg/150px-TD_Six_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/TD_Six_2003.jpg/225px-TD_Six_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/TD_Six_2003.jpg/300px-TD_Six_2003.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:6-L_2003_track.png"><img alt="6-L 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/6-L_2003_track.png/150px-6-L_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/6-L_2003_track.png/225px-6-L_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/6-L_2003_track.png/300px-6-L_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 19 – July 21</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1010 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved westward off the coast of Africa on July 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td6tcr_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-td6tcr-42">[42]</a></sup> After tracking steadily westward, an area of thunderstorms became more concentrated as its upper-level environment became more favorable,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and late on July 19 the National Hurricane Center classified it as Tropical Depression Six while it was located about 1035 mi (1675 km) east of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td6tcr_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-td6tcr-42">[42]</a></sup> Upon being classified as a tropical cyclone, the depression maintained two ill-defined <a href="/wiki/Squall#Tropical_cyclones" title="Squall">hooking bands</a> to its north and south, and was originally forecast to attain hurricane status before passing through the Lesser Antilles. With warm waters and very light wind shear forecast, its environmental conditions met four out of five parameters for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid intensification</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td6disc1_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-td6disc1-44">[44]</a></sup> Subsequently, convection diminished as the result of cold air <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Physical_structure" title="Tropical cyclone">inflow</a> and instability from a disturbance to its southeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>With a fast forward speed, confirmation of a low-level circulation on July 20 became difficult.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Convection increased in curvature on July 21,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and several islands in the Lesser Antilles issued <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">tropical storm warnings and watches</a>. After it passed north of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hunters" title="Hurricane Hunters">Hurricane Hunters</a> flight failed to report a closed low-level circulation, and it is estimated the depression degenerated into an open tropical wave late on July 21. The remnants brought a few showers to the Lesser Antilles,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td6tcr_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-td6tcr-42">[42]</a></sup> and after tracking into the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> redevelopment was prevented by increased wind shear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The northern portion of the wave axis split and developed into Tropical Depression Seven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td6tcr_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-td6tcr-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Seven">Tropical Depression Seven</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Seven">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1016 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave interacted with an upper-level low to develop an area of deep convection near <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> on July 23.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td7tcr_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-td7tcr-49">[49]</a></sup> A mid- to lower-level circulation developed within the system at it tracked generally north-northwestward, and based on surface and satellite observations, it is estimated the system developed into Tropical Depression Seven at 1200 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on July 25 about 60 mi (95 km) east of <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach,_Florida" title="Daytona Beach, Florida">Daytona Beach</a>, Florida. The system was embedded in an environment characterized by high surface pressures. Tracking through an area of cool water temperatures,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td7tcr_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-td7tcr-49">[49]</a></sup> as well as unfavorable upper-level winds, the depression failed to achieve winds greater than 35 mph (55 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early on July 26 it moved ashore on <a href="/wiki/St._Catherines_Island" title="St. Catherines Island">St. Catherines Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, and after steadily weakening over land it dissipated on July 27. As the storm was never forecast to attain tropical storm status, no <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">tropical storm warnings or watches</a> were issued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td7tcr_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-td7tcr-49">[49]</a></sup> However, flood watches were posted for much of Georgia and <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The depression dropped light to moderate rainfall from Florida to the coast of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, peaking at 5.17 in (131 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>. Mostly, rainfall totals between 1 and 3 inches (25 and 76 mm) were common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> There were no reports of damage or casualties associated with this depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td7tcr_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-td7tcr-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Erika">Hurricane Erika</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hurricane Erika">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erika_Aug_16_2003_1655Z.jpg"><img alt="Erika Aug 16 2003 1655Z.jpg" data-file-height="5834" data-file-width="5232" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Erika_Aug_16_2003_1655Z.jpg/150px-Erika_Aug_16_2003_1655Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Erika_Aug_16_2003_1655Z.jpg/225px-Erika_Aug_16_2003_1655Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Erika_Aug_16_2003_1655Z.jpg/300px-Erika_Aug_16_2003_1655Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erika_2003_track.png"><img alt="Erika 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Erika_2003_track.png/150px-Erika_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Erika_2003_track.png/225px-Erika_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Erika_2003_track.png/300px-Erika_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 14 – August 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>75 mph (120 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  986 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Erika_(2003)" title="Hurricane Erika (2003)">Hurricane Erika (2003)</a></div>
<p>The precursor system to Hurricane Erika was first observed as a non-tropical low on August 9 about 1150 mi (1860 km) east of Bermuda. It tracked quickly southwestward then westward in tandem with an upper-level low, which prevented tropical development. On August 13 an area of convection increased as it passed through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, and while crossing Florida a circulation built toward the surface; it is estimated the system developed into Tropical Storm Erika on August 14 about 85 mi (140 km) west-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Myers,_Florida" title="Fort Myers, Florida">Fort Myers</a>, Florida. A strong <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a> caused the storm to continue quickly westward, and the system gradually strengthened and organized. By August 15 its forward motion slowed, allowing the convection to organize into curved <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Physical_structure" title="Tropical cyclone">rainbands</a>, and late in the day an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye feature</a> began developing. Tropical Storm Erika attained hurricane status at around 1030 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> as it was moving ashore in northeastern Tamaulipas; operationally it was not classified as a hurricane, due to lack of data. The winds rapidly decreased as it tracked across the mountainous terrain of northeastern <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and early on August 17 the cyclone dissipated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-erikatcr_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-erikatcr-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The hurricane dropped light to moderate rainfall along its path, which caused some flooding; in <a href="/wiki/Montemorelos" title="Montemorelos">Montemorelos</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Le%C3%B3n" title="Nuevo León">Nuevo León</a>, two people died after being swept away by floodwaters. Several mudslides were reported, which left numerous highways blocked or impassable. In southern Texas, the hurricane caused light winds and minor damage, with no reports of deaths or injuries in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-erikatcr_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-erikatcr-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Nine">Tropical Depression Nine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Nine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_9_22_aug_2003_1215Z.jpg"><img alt="TD 9 22 aug 2003 1215Z.jpg" data-file-height="898" data-file-width="898" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/TD_9_22_aug_2003_1215Z.jpg/150px-TD_9_22_aug_2003_1215Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/TD_9_22_aug_2003_1215Z.jpg/225px-TD_9_22_aug_2003_1215Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/TD_9_22_aug_2003_1215Z.jpg/300px-TD_9_22_aug_2003_1215Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:9-L_2003_track.png"><img alt="9-L 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/9-L_2003_track.png/150px-9-L_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/9-L_2003_track.png/225px-9-L_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/9-L_2003_track.png/300px-9-L_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 21 – August 22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1007 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Depression_Nine_(2003)" title="Tropical Depression Nine (2003)">Tropical Depression Nine (2003)</a></div>
<p>A strong <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of Africa on August 14,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td9tcr_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-td9tcr-54">[54]</a></sup> and after tracking steadily westward an area of convection began to become better organized on August 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aug18two2_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-aug18two2-55">[55]</a></sup> After it tracked through the Lesser Antilles, it developed into Tropical Depression Nine on August 21 to the south of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. The depression quickly showed signs of organization, and forecasters predicted the depression to intensify to a strong tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td9disc1_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-td9disc1-56">[56]</a></sup> However, strong southwesterly <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> unexpectedly became established over the system, and the depression degenerated into a tropical wave late on August 22 to the south of the eastern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td9tcr_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-td9tcr-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>The remnants of the depression dropped light to moderate precipitation in the Dominican Republic, which caused flooding and overflown rivers. More than 100 houses were flooded, and some crop damage was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003wmo_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-2003wmo-15">[15]</a></sup> The rainfall was welcome in the country, as conditions were dry in the preceding months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-domrep_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-domrep-57">[57]</a></sup> Flooding was also reported in eastern <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, though damage there, if any, is unknown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003wmo_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-2003wmo-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Fabian">Hurricane Fabian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Hurricane Fabian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_fabian_2003.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane fabian 2003.jpg" data-file-height="5200" data-file-width="5200" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hurricane_fabian_2003.jpg/150px-Hurricane_fabian_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hurricane_fabian_2003.jpg/225px-Hurricane_fabian_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hurricane_fabian_2003.jpg/300px-Hurricane_fabian_2003.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fabian_2003_track.png"><img alt="Fabian 2003 track.png" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Fabian_2003_track.png/150px-Fabian_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Fabian_2003_track.png/225px-Fabian_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Fabian_2003_track.png/300px-Fabian_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 27 – September 8</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>145 mph (230 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  939 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fabian" title="Hurricane Fabian">Hurricane Fabian</a></div>
<p>On August 25, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> emerged off the coast of Africa, and two days later developed enough organized convection to develop into Tropical Depression Ten. Tracking through warm waters and low vertical shear, the depression was named Tropical Storm Fabian on August 28. On August 30, the storm intensified into a hurricane, and it quickly strengthened to attain major hurricane status late that day; on September 1 Fabian reached its peak intensity of 145 mph (230 km/h). The hurricane turned to the north and gradually weakened before passing 14 mi (23 km) west of Bermuda on September 5 with winds of 115 mph (180 km/h). The cyclone accelerated northeastward into an environment of unfavorable conditions, becoming an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> on September 8; two days later it merged with another extratropical storm between southern <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fabiantcr_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-fabiantcr-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Strong waves caused extensive damage to the Bermuda coastline,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003wmo_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-2003wmo-15">[15]</a></sup> destroying 10 nests of the endangered <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_petrel" title="Bermuda petrel">Bermuda petrel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-berpetrel_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-berpetrel-58">[58]</a></sup> The storm surge from the hurricane stranded one vehicle with three police officers and another with a resident on <a href="/wiki/The_Causeway,_Bermuda" title="The Causeway, Bermuda">the causeway</a> between <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Parish,_Bermuda" title="St. George's Parish, Bermuda">St. George's Parish</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._David%27s_Island,_Bermuda" title="St. David's Island, Bermuda">St. David's Island</a>, later washing both vehicles into <a href="/wiki/Castle_Harbour,_Bermuda" title="Castle Harbour, Bermuda">Castle Harbour</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rgsearching_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-rgsearching-59">[59]</a></sup> all four were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fabiantcr_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-fabiantcr-22">[22]</a></sup> Strong winds left about 25,000 people without power on the island, and also caused severe damage to vegetation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003wmo_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-2003wmo-15">[15]</a></sup> The strong winds damaged or destroyed the roofs of numerous buildings on Bermuda,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shorts_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-shorts-60">[60]</a></sup> Damage on the island totaled $300 million (2003 USD, $391 million 2017 USD). Elsewhere, strong waves from the hurricane killed a surfer in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> and caused three deaths off of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland</a> when a fishing vessel sank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fabiantcr_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-fabiantcr-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Grace">Tropical Storm Grace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Grace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grace_30_August_2003.jpg"><img alt="Grace 30 August 2003.jpg" data-file-height="1100" data-file-width="1187" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Grace_30_August_2003.jpg/150px-Grace_30_August_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Grace_30_August_2003.jpg/225px-Grace_30_August_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Grace_30_August_2003.jpg/300px-Grace_30_August_2003.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grace_2003_track.png"><img alt="Grace 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Grace_2003_track.png/150px-Grace_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Grace_2003_track.png/225px-Grace_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Grace_2003_track.png/300px-Grace_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 30 – September 2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>40 mph (65 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1007 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Grace_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Grace (2003)">Tropical Storm Grace (2003)</a></div>
<p>A strong <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> accompanied with a low pressure system moved off the coast of Africa on August 19. It moved quickly westward, failing to organize significantly, and developed a surface <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a> on August 29 in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>. Convection continued to organize, and the tropical wave developed into Tropical Depression Eleven on August 30 while located 335 mi (540 km) east-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi,_Texas" title="Corpus Christi, Texas">Corpus Christi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>. The depression quickly intensified to become Tropical Storm Grace, though further intensification was limited due to a nearby upper-level low. On August 31, Grace moved ashore on <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">Galveston Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, and it quickly weakened over land. The storm turned northeastward and was absorbed by a <a href="/wiki/Cold_front" title="Cold front">cold front</a> over extreme eastern <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a> on September 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gracetcr_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-gracetcr-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>The storm produced light to moderate precipitation from Texas through the eastern United States, peaking at 10.4 in (263 mm) in eastern Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grain_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-grain-62">[62]</a></sup> Near where it made landfall, Grace produced flooding of low-lying areas and light beach erosion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jambeach_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-jambeach-63">[63]</a></sup> In Oklahoma and southern <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>, the remnants of the storm caused localized flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oklanws_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-oklanws-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paducnws_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-paducnws-65">[65]</a></sup> No deaths were reported, and damage was minimal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gracetcr_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-gracetcr-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
