</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Henri_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Henri (2003)">Tropical Storm Henri (2003)</a></div>
<p>On August 22, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of Africa, and it remained disorganized until reaching the eastern Gulf of Mexico on September 1. A tropical disturbance developed into Tropical Depression Twelve on September 3 about 300 mi (480 km) west of <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>. It moved eastward and strengthened into Tropical Storm Henri on September 5, and despite strong <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> it intensified to reach peak winds of 60 mph (95 km/h) later that day. Subsequently, it quickly weakened, and it struck the western Florida coast as a tropical depression. On September 8 it degenerated into a remnant low pressure area off the coast of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-henritcr_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-henritcr-66">[66]</a></sup> and after moving ashore near <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras" title="Cape Hatteras">Cape Hatteras</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-two12_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-two12-67">[67]</a></sup> it crossed the Mid-Atlantic states and dissipated on September 17 over <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wpc_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-wpc-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Henri was responsible for locally heavy rainfall across Florida, but damage was minimal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-henritcr_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-henritcr-66">[66]</a></sup> The remnants of Henri caused heavy precipitation in <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, causing $19.6 million in damage (2003 USD; $24.7 million 2017 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dedam_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-dedam-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pedam_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-pedam-70">[70]</a></sup> In Delaware, the rainfall caused record-breaking river flooding, with part of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Clay_Creek" title="Red Clay Creek">Red Clay Creek</a> experiencing a <a href="/wiki/100-year_flood" title="100-year flood">500-year flood</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deriv_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-deriv-71">[71]</a></sup> and the system left 109,000 residents without power in Pennsylvania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pedam_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-pedam-70">[70]</a></sup> The impacts of the storm were severely compounded the following week by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isabel" title="Hurricane Isabel">Hurricane Isabel</a> across the region.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Isabel">Hurricane Isabel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hurricane Isabel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_isabel2_2003.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane isabel2 2003.jpg" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="6000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hurricane_isabel2_2003.jpg/150px-Hurricane_isabel2_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hurricane_isabel2_2003.jpg/225px-Hurricane_isabel2_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hurricane_isabel2_2003.jpg/300px-Hurricane_isabel2_2003.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isabel_2003_track.png"><img alt="Isabel 2003 track.png" data-file-height="766" data-file-width="1024" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Isabel_2003_track.png/150px-Isabel_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Isabel_2003_track.png/225px-Isabel_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Isabel_2003_track.png/300px-Isabel_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 6 – September 19</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>165 mph (270 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  915 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isabel" title="Hurricane Isabel">Hurricane Isabel</a></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of Africa on September 1, which developed into Tropical Depression Thirteen early on September 6 to the southwest of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> islands. It quickly intensified into Tropical Storm Isabel,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-istcr_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-istcr-17">[17]</a></sup> and it continued to gradually intensify within an area of light <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> and warm waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disco2_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-disco2-72">[72]</a></sup> Isabel strengthened to a hurricane on September 7, and the following day it attained <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane status</a>. Its intensity fluctuated over the subsequent days as it passed north of the Lesser Antilles, and it attained peak winds of 165 mph (270 km/h) on September 11, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">Category 5 hurricane</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Scale</a>. The hurricane oscillated between Category 4 and Category 5 status over the following four days, before weakening due to wind shear. On September 18 Isabel made landfall between <a href="/wiki/Cape_Lookout_(North_Carolina)" title="Cape Lookout (North Carolina)">Cape Lookout</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocracoke_Island" title="Ocracoke Island">Ocracoke Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> with winds of 105 mph (165 km/h). It continued northwestward, becoming <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> over western <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> before being absorbed by a larger storm over <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> on September 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-istcr_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-istcr-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Strong winds from Isabel extended from <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> to <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> and westward to <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>. The winds, combined with previous rainfall which moistened the soil, downed many trees and power lines across its path, leaving about 6 million electricity customers without power at some point. Coastal areas suffered from waves and its powerful storm surge, with areas in eastern North Carolina and southeast <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> reporting severe damage from both winds and the storm surge. Throughout its path, Isabel resulted in $3.6 billion in damage (2003 USD; $4.69 billion 2017 USD) and 47 deaths, of which 16 were directly related to the storm's effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assess_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-assess-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The governors of <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> declared states of emergencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scotsman_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-scotsman-73">[73]</a></sup> Isabel was the first major hurricane to threaten the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_States" title="Mid-Atlantic States">Mid-Atlantic States</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Southern_States" title="U.S. Southern States">South</a> since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" title="Hurricane Floyd">Hurricane Floyd</a> in September 1999. Isabel's greatest impact was due to <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">flood</a> damage, the worst in some areas of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> since 1972's <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Agnes" title="Hurricane Agnes">Hurricane Agnes</a>. More than 60 million people were affected to some degree — a similar number to Floyd but more than any other hurricane in recent memory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdcisfl_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdcisfl-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Fourteen">Tropical Depression Fourteen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Fourteen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TD_14_09_sept_2003_1445Z.jpg"><img alt="TD 14 09 sept 2003 1445Z.jpg" data-file-height="898" data-file-width="898" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/TD_14_09_sept_2003_1445Z.jpg/150px-TD_14_09_sept_2003_1445Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/TD_14_09_sept_2003_1445Z.jpg/225px-TD_14_09_sept_2003_1445Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/TD_14_09_sept_2003_1445Z.jpg/300px-TD_14_09_sept_2003_1445Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:14-L_2003_track.png"><img alt="14-L 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/14-L_2003_track.png/150px-14-L_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/14-L_2003_track.png/225px-14-L_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/14-L_2003_track.png/300px-14-L_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 8 – September 10</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1007 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A strong <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of Africa on September 6, and almost immediately it became associated with a broad surface circulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td14tcr_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-td14tcr-75">[75]</a></sup> With favorable upper-level winds the system quickly became better organized,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> and on September 8 it possessed enough organization to be classified as Tropical Depression Fourteen while located about 290 mi (465 km) southeast of the southernmost <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td14tcr_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-td14tcr-75">[75]</a></sup> Initially the depression failed to maintain an inner core of deep convection, and despite its occurrence with nearby dry air, the depression was forecast to intensify to hurricane status due to anticipated favorable conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td14disc1_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-td14disc1-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the hours subsequent to formation, the convection near the center decreased as the banding features dissipated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Dry air greatly increased over the depression, and by September 9 the system was not forecast to intensify past minimal tropical storm status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Later that day an upper-level low tracked southward to the west of the depression, which increased wind shear and caused a steady north-northwest motion for the depression. The circulation became elongated and separated from the convection as it passed just west of the Cape Verde Islands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td14tcr_75-2"><a href="#cite_note-td14tcr-75">[75]</a></sup> where it brought heavy rainfall,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> and on September 10 the depression dissipated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td14tcr_75-3"><a href="#cite_note-td14tcr-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Juan">Hurricane Juan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hurricane Juan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Juan_27_sept_2003_1725Z.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane Juan 27 sept 2003 1725Z.jpg" data-file-height="6800" data-file-width="5200" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Hurricane_Juan_27_sept_2003_1725Z.jpg/150px-Hurricane_Juan_27_sept_2003_1725Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Hurricane_Juan_27_sept_2003_1725Z.jpg/225px-Hurricane_Juan_27_sept_2003_1725Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Hurricane_Juan_27_sept_2003_1725Z.jpg/300px-Hurricane_Juan_27_sept_2003_1725Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Juan_2003_track.png"><img alt="Juan 2003 track.png" data-file-height="719" data-file-width="1024" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Juan_2003_track.png/150px-Juan_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Juan_2003_track.png/225px-Juan_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Juan_2003_track.png/300px-Juan_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 24 – September 29</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>105 mph (165 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  969 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Juan" title="Hurricane Juan">Hurricane Juan</a></div>
<p>A large <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of Africa on September 14,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juantcr_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-juantcr-81">[81]</a></sup> and due to unfavorable <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> it initially remained disorganized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sept17two_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-sept17two-82">[82]</a></sup> An area of convection increased in association with an upper-level low, and it developed into Tropical Depression Fifteen on September 24 to the southeast of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>. It steadily organized as it tracked northward, intensifying into Tropical Storm Juan on September 25 and attaining hurricane status on September 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juantcr_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-juantcr-81">[81]</a></sup> With warm waters and light wind shear, Juan reached peak winds of 105 mph (165 km/h) on September 27 about 635 mi (1,020 km) south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax</a>, Nova Scotia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avila10_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-avila10-83">[83]</a></sup> It accelerated northward, weakening only slightly before moving ashore near Halifax on September 29 with winds of 100 mph (160 km/h). It quickly weakened while crossing the southern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Maritimes" title="Canadian Maritimes">Canadian Maritimes</a> before being absorbed by a large <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">Gulf of Saint Lawrence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juantcr_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-juantcr-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The eyewall of Hurricane Juan was the first to directly cross over Halifax since a hurricane in August of <a href="/wiki/1893_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1893 Atlantic hurricane season">1893</a>; the cyclone became one of the most damaging tropical cyclones in modern history for the city. The hurricane produced a record <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> of 4.9 ft (1.5 m), which resulted in extensive flooding of the Halifax and Dartmouth waterfront properties. Strong winds caused widespread occurrences of falling trees, downed power lines, and damaged houses, and the hurricane was responsible for four direct deaths and four indirect deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juantcr_81-3"><a href="#cite_note-juantcr-81">[81]</a></sup> More than 800,000 people were left without power. Nearly all wind-related damage occurred to the east of the storm track, and damage amounted to about $200 million (2003 <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">CAD</a>; $150 million 2003 USD; $260 million 2017 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-summary_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-summary-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Kate">Hurricane Kate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Hurricane Kate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_kate_2003.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane kate 2003.jpg" data-file-height="5200" data-file-width="5200" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hurricane_kate_2003.jpg/150px-Hurricane_kate_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hurricane_kate_2003.jpg/225px-Hurricane_kate_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hurricane_kate_2003.jpg/300px-Hurricane_kate_2003.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kate_2003_track.png"><img alt="Kate 2003 track.png" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Kate_2003_track.png/150px-Kate_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Kate_2003_track.png/225px-Kate_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Kate_2003_track.png/300px-Kate_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 25 – October 7</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>125 mph (205 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  952 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Kate_(2003)" title="Hurricane Kate (2003)">Hurricane Kate (2003)</a></div>
<p>Kate developed from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> in the central tropical Atlantic on September 25. The storm moved northwestward until a weakness in the <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">subtropical ridge</a> forced it eastward. Kate strengthened to a hurricane, turned sharply westward while moving around a mid-level low, and intensified to a 125 mph (205 km/h) major hurricane on October 4. Kate turned sharply northward around the periphery of an <a href="/wiki/Anticyclone" title="Anticyclone">anticyclone</a>, weakened, and became extratropical after passing to the east of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>. The extratropical storm persisted for three days until losing its identity near <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katetcr_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-katetcr-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kate threatened <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a> just one week after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Juan" title="Hurricane Juan">Hurricane Juan</a> caused severe damage in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>. The storm had minimal effects on land, limited to moderately strong winds and heavy rainfall over Newfoundland;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katebulletin3_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-katebulletin3-85">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="St. John's, Newfoundland and Labrador">St. John's</a> reported 1.8 in (45 mm) on October 6, a record for the date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbcnews_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbcnews-86">[86]</a></sup> The interaction between Kate and a high pressure area to its north produced three to four ft (one m) waves along the coast of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-surfline_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-surfline-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Larry">Tropical Storm Larry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Larry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Larry_05_oct_2003_1645Z.jpg"><img alt="TS Larry 05 oct 2003 1645Z.jpg" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="4000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/TS_Larry_05_oct_2003_1645Z.jpg/150px-TS_Larry_05_oct_2003_1645Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/TS_Larry_05_oct_2003_1645Z.jpg/225px-TS_Larry_05_oct_2003_1645Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/TS_Larry_05_oct_2003_1645Z.jpg/300px-TS_Larry_05_oct_2003_1645Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Larry_2003_track.png"><img alt="Larry 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Larry_2003_track.png/150px-Larry_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Larry_2003_track.png/225px-Larry_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Larry_2003_track.png/300px-Larry_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 1 – October 6</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 mph (100 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  993 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Larry" title="Tropical Storm Larry">Tropical Storm Larry</a></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of Africa on September 17, which developed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a> on September 27 in the western <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. It moved ashore along the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a> on September 29 and developed into an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> as it interacted with a stationary <a href="/wiki/Cold_front" title="Cold front">cold front</a>. Deep convection increased, and it transitioned into Tropical Storm Larry by October 1. The storm drifted generally southward, and after reaching peak winds of 65 mph (100 km/h) it made landfall in the <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexican</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Tabasco" title="Tabasco">Tabasco</a> on October 5,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-larrytcr_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-larrytcr-88">[88]</a></sup> the first landfall in the state since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Brenda_(1973)" title="Hurricane Brenda (1973)">Hurricane Brenda</a> in 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mexgob_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-mexgob-89">[89]</a></sup> The remnants of Larry crossed the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Tehuantepec" title="Isthmus of Tehuantepec">Isthmus of Tehuantepec</a>, degenerating into a remnant low pressure area before dissipating on October 7 in the eastern Pacific Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-larrytcr_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-larrytcr-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>The storm dropped heavy rainfall, peaking at 24.77 inches (629.2 mm) in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Upper_Juarez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Upper Juarez (page does not exist)">Upper Juarez</a> in southeastern <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-larain_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-larain-90">[90]</a></sup> The rainfall caused mudslides and damage, which coincided with the presence of two other tropical cyclones – Eastern Pacific tropical storm Nora and Olaf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aplar_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-aplar-91">[91]</a></sup> Overall, the storm resulted in five deaths and $53.4 million in damage (2003 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-larrytcr_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-larrytcr-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zuniga_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-zuniga-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Mindy">Tropical Storm Mindy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Mindy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Storm_Mindy_(2003)_MODIS_Peak.JPG"><img alt="Tropical Storm Mindy (2003) MODIS Peak.JPG" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="651" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Tropical_Storm_Mindy_%282003%29_MODIS_Peak.JPG/150px-Tropical_Storm_Mindy_%282003%29_MODIS_Peak.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Tropical_Storm_Mindy_%282003%29_MODIS_Peak.JPG/225px-Tropical_Storm_Mindy_%282003%29_MODIS_Peak.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Tropical_Storm_Mindy_%282003%29_MODIS_Peak.JPG/300px-Tropical_Storm_Mindy_%282003%29_MODIS_Peak.JPG 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mindy_2003_track.png"><img alt="Mindy 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mindy_2003_track.png/150px-Mindy_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mindy_2003_track.png/225px-Mindy_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mindy_2003_track.png/300px-Mindy_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 10 – October 14</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> exited the coast of Africa on October 1 and moved westward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtcr_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtcr-93">[93]</a></sup> On October 8, thunderstorms spread across the Lesser Antilles, and the wave slowly organized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oct8two_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-oct8two-94">[94]</a></sup> Rainfall reached 2.98 in (75 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Christiansted,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Christiansted, U.S. Virgin Islands">Christiansted</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Croix, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Croix</a>, and 7.13 in (181 mm) near <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce, Puerto Rico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mrain_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-mrain-95">[95]</a></sup> Strong winds left around 29,000 people without power in northeastern Puerto Rico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc6_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc6-96">[96]</a></sup> The rainfall wrecked bridges in <a href="/wiki/Las_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="Las Piedras, Puerto Rico">Las Piedras</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guayama" title="Guayama">Guayama</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc8_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc8-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc12_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc12-98">[98]</a></sup> and led to flooded streams, downed trees, and rockslides that closed four roads. One car was swept away,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc3_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc3-99">[99]</a></sup> and a few houses were flooded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc4_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc4-100">[100]</a></sup> The damage total was at least $46,000 (2003 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc8_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc8-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc12_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc12-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc11_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc11-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>It turned northwestward through a weakness in the <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">subtropical ridge</a>, and despite strong wind shear developed into Tropical Storm Mindy late on October 10 over eastern <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, with peak winds of 45 mph (75 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtcr_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtcr-93">[93]</a></sup> It produced 2.63 in (60 mm) of rain in <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Province" title="Santiago Rodríguez Province">Santiago Rodríguez</a>, which caused flooding and damaged 320 houses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmo_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-wmo-102">[102]</a></sup> Although forecast to intensify to 65 mph (105 km/h) winds, the storm weakened due to the wind shear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mindydisc2_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-mindydisc2-103">[103]</a></sup> The center passed near the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a> on October 11,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtcr_93-2"><a href="#cite_note-mtcr-93">[93]</a></sup> and winds reached only 31 mph (50 km/h) at <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">Grand Turk Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmo_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-wmo-102">[102]</a></sup> On October 12, Mindy weakened to a tropical depression, and later turned eastward due to an approaching short-wave <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">trough</a>. Devoid of deep convection, the circulation dissipated on October 14 about 445 mi (715 km) south-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtcr_93-3"><a href="#cite_note-mtcr-93">[93]</a></sup> Mindy produced two to three ft (0.6 to 0.9 m) swells along the U.S. Atlantic coast from <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> through <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-surfline_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-surfline-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Nicholas">Tropical Storm Nicholas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Nicholas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Nicholas_17_oct_2003_1345Z.jpg"><img alt="TS Nicholas 17 oct 2003 1345Z.jpg" data-file-height="852" data-file-width="992" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/TS_Nicholas_17_oct_2003_1345Z.jpg/150px-TS_Nicholas_17_oct_2003_1345Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/TS_Nicholas_17_oct_2003_1345Z.jpg/225px-TS_Nicholas_17_oct_2003_1345Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/TS_Nicholas_17_oct_2003_1345Z.jpg/300px-TS_Nicholas_17_oct_2003_1345Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicholas_2003_track.png"><img alt="Nicholas 2003 track.png" data-file-height="751" data-file-width="1024" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Nicholas_2003_track.png/150px-Nicholas_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Nicholas_2003_track.png/225px-Nicholas_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Nicholas_2003_track.png/300px-Nicholas_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 13 – October 23</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>70 mph (110 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  990 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Nicholas" title="Tropical Storm Nicholas">Tropical Storm Nicholas</a></div>
<p>Forming from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> on October 13 in the central tropical <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, Nicholas slowly developed due to moderate levels of wind shear throughout its lifetime. Deep convection slowly organized, and Nicholas attained a peak intensity of 70 mph (110 km/h) on October 17. After moving west-northwestward for much of its lifetime, it turned northward and weakened due to increasing shear. The storm again turned to the west and briefly restrengthened, but after turning again to the north Nicholas transitioned to an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extratropical" title="Extratropical">extratropical</a> cyclone on October 24. As an extratropical storm, Nicholas executed a large loop to the west, and after moving erratically for a week and organizing into a tropical low, it was absorbed by a non-tropical low. The low continued westward, crossed <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, and ultimately dissipated over the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">Gulf Coast of the United States</a> on November 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nictcr_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-nictcr-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nicholas had no impact as a tropical cyclone, and impact from the low that absorbed the storm was limited to rainfall, gusty winds, and rough surf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The low that absorbed the storm nearly developed into a tropical cyclone, which would have been called Odette. However, moderate <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> prevented further development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nov2003summary_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-nov2003summary-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Odette">Tropical Storm Odette</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Odette">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Odette_6_December_2003.jpg"><img alt="Odette 6 December 2003.jpg" data-file-height="10606" data-file-width="9208" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Odette_6_December_2003.jpg/150px-Odette_6_December_2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Odette_6_December_2003.jpg/225px-Odette_6_December_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Odette_6_December_2003.jpg/300px-Odette_6_December_2003.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Odette_2003_track.png"><img alt="Odette 2003 track.png" data-file-height="1740" data-file-width="2700" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Odette_2003_track.png/150px-Odette_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Odette_2003_track.png/225px-Odette_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Odette_2003_track.png/300px-Odette_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>December 4 – December 7</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 mph (100 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  993 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Odette_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Odette (2003)">Tropical Storm Odette (2003)</a></div>
<p>Odette was a rare December tropical storm, the first since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lili_(1984)" title="Hurricane Lili (1984)">Hurricane Lili</a> in 1984, that formed on December 4 in the southwest Caribbean Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odettetcr_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-odettetcr-12">[12]</a></sup> It became the second December tropical storm on record to form in the Caribbean Sea, after a hurricane in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1820-1829_Atlantic_hurricane_seasons#1822_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1820-1829 Atlantic hurricane seasons">1822</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odettetcr_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-odettetcr-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Odette strengthened and made landfall near <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cabo_Falso&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cabo Falso (page does not exist)">Cabo Falso</a> in the Dominican Republic on December 6 as a moderately strong tropical storm. A day later, Odette became extratropical, and eventually merged with a cold front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odettetcr_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-odettetcr-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eight deaths were directly attributed to this tropical storm in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> due to mudslides or flash flooding. In addition, two deaths were indirectly caused by the storm. Approximately 35% of the nation's <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a> crop was destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odettetcr_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-odettetcr-12">[12]</a></sup> Light to moderate rainfall was reported in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Peter">Tropical Storm Peter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Peter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peter_Dec_9_2003_1535Z.jpg"><img alt="Peter Dec 9 2003 1535Z.jpg" data-file-height="6081" data-file-width="5778" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Peter_Dec_9_2003_1535Z.jpg/150px-Peter_Dec_9_2003_1535Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Peter_Dec_9_2003_1535Z.jpg/225px-Peter_Dec_9_2003_1535Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Peter_Dec_9_2003_1535Z.jpg/300px-Peter_Dec_9_2003_1535Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peter_2003_track.png"><img alt="Peter 2003 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Peter_2003_track.png/150px-Peter_2003_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Peter_2003_track.png/225px-Peter_2003_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Peter_2003_track.png/300px-Peter_2003_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>December 7 – December 11</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>70 mph (110 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  990 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-season_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of off-season Atlantic hurricanes">List of off-season Atlantic hurricanes</a></div>
<p>By December 5, an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> developed and was moving southward, isolated from the <a href="/wiki/Westerlies" title="Westerlies">Westerlies</a>. Convection developed near the center, and the system organized into a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical storm</a> late on December 7, about 835 mi (1340 km) south-southwest of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>. The system moved southwestward over warmer waters, and deep convection continued to organize over the center. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rainbands" title="Rainbands">Banding features</a> also increased, and the National Hurricane Center declared the system as Tropical Storm Peter on December 9, about 980 mi (1580 km) northwest of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> islands. With the development of Peter and Odette, 2003 became the first year since <a href="/wiki/1887_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1887 Atlantic hurricane season">1887</a> that two storms developed in the month of December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptcr_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-ptcr-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially, the National Hurricane Center did not anticipate strengthening;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-peterdisc1_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-peterdisc1-109">[109]</a></sup> however, Peter intensified to winds of 70 mph (110 km/h) late on December 9, after an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye feature</a> developed. Usually that would indicate hurricane intensity, but as the eye was short-lived, Peter remained a tropical storm. It turned northward ahead of the same <a href="/wiki/Cold_front" title="Cold front">frontal system</a> that absorbed <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Odette_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Odette (2003)">Tropical Storm Odette</a>, and the combination of strong upper-level winds and cooler water temperatures caused quick weakening. By December 10, Peter degenerated into a tropical depression, and after turning northeastward it was absorbed by the cold front the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ptcr_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-ptcr-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This is a table of all of the storms that have formed during the 2003 Atlantic hurricane season. It includes their names, duration, peak strength, areas affected, damage, and death totals. Deaths in parentheses are additional and indirect (an example of an indirect death would be a traffic accident), but were still related to that storm. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical, a wave, or a low, and all of the damage figures are in 2003 USD.</p>

</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names" title="List of historic tropical cyclone names">List of historic tropical cyclone names</a></div>
<p>The following names were used for named storms that formed in the North Atlantic in 2003. The names not retired from this list were used again in the <a href="/wiki/2009_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2009 Atlantic hurricane season">2009 season</a>. This is the same list used for the <a href="/wiki/1997_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1997 Atlantic hurricane season">1997 season</a>. Storms were named Larry, Mindy, Nicholas, Odette, and Peter for the first time in 2003. Names that were not assigned are marked in <span style="color:#666666">gray</span>. Ana became the first name in the six list rotation to be used five times. Both Ana and Claudette were used in 1979, 1985, 1991, 1997, 2003, 2009 and 2015.</p>
<table style="width:80%;">
<tr>
<td>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)">Ana</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bill_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Bill (2003)">Bill</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Claudette_(2003)" title="Hurricane Claudette (2003)">Claudette</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Danny_(2003)" title="Hurricane Danny (2003)">Danny</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Erika_(2003)" title="Hurricane Erika (2003)">Erika</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fabian" title="Hurricane Fabian">Fabian</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Grace_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Grace (2003)">Grace</a></li>
</ul>
</td>

<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Juan" title="Hurricane Juan">Juan</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Kate_(2003)" title="Hurricane Kate (2003)">Kate</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Larry_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Larry (2003)">Larry</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Atlantic_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Atlantic hurricane names">List of retired Atlantic hurricane names</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> retired three names in the spring of 2004: Fabian, Isabel, and Juan. They were replaced in the <a href="/wiki/2009_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2009 Atlantic hurricane season">2009 season</a> by Fred, Ida, and Joaquin, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003wmo_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-2003wmo-15">[15]</a></sup> The name Joaquin was not used in 2009 but instead was used in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2015 Atlantic hurricane season">2015 season</a>; Joaquin was then retired in 2015 and replaced by Julian for the 2021 season.</p>
